## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws describing elastic, plastic, and thermoelastic response of materials with temperature-dependent stiffness and strength (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (small-strain elastic response with coefficient of thermal expansion)
- Temperature-dependent Young’s modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear softening/stiffening of modulus with temperature)
- Reciprocal modulus softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 / (T + c2)) * epsilon (stiffness decreases with temperature in a bounded way)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (weakly nonlinear elasticity with T-dependent coefficients)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-like uniaxial surrogate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 / (1 + c3 * epsilon)) (captures stiffening as strain grows; surrogate form for large-strain behavior)
- Hollomon strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (power-law hardening with multiplicative temperature dependence)
- Ludwik-type law with temperature-dependent yield offset: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) * epsilon**c4 (yield/flow stress plus hardening; both temperature dependent)
- Voce-type saturation hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) * (1 - exp(-(c4 * exp(c5 * T)) * epsilon)) (hardening saturates at large strain; saturation rate depends on T)
- Kocks–Mecking-like hardening (rational saturation): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * epsilon) / (1 + (c3 * exp(c4 * T)) * epsilon) (initial hardening that gradually saturates; T shifts the saturation strain)
- Logarithmic hardening (true-stress-like surrogate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) * log(1 + c4 * epsilon) (common empirical form when hardening slows with strain)
- Thermally activated flow stress (Eyring-like surrogate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * asinh((c3 * epsilon) * exp(c4 / (T + c5))) (captures strong temperature sensitivity consistent with thermally activated mechanisms)
- Ramberg–Osgood inversion surrogate (stress as function of strain): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + (c2 * exp(c3 * T)) * Abs(epsilon)**c4) (smoothly transitions from linear elastic to nonlinear/plastic-like response)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion compensation: if heating causes stress drop at fixed total strain, try sigma depending on an effective strain (epsilon - c * (T - c0)) rather than on epsilon alone.
- Temperature-dependent modulus/strength: encode thermal softening by making coefficients multiplying epsilon or epsilon**n decrease with T (e.g., linear-in-T or exp(c*T) prefactors).
- Elastic regime signature: near epsilon ≈ 0, sigma is often approximately linear in epsilon with slope set by a T-dependent modulus.
- Strain hardening signature: curvature in sigma–epsilon suggests power-law (epsilon**n) or log(1 + c*epsilon) terms; slowing hardening at large strain suggests saturating exponentials or rational saturation.
- Yield/flow stress offset: nonzero intercept (sigma at small but finite epsilon) can be modeled by an additive term that depends on T (thermal softening of yield stress).
- Bounded high-strain behavior: if sigma approaches an asymptote with increasing epsilon, use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or epsilon/(1 + c*epsilon) structures with T-dependent rates.
- Strong temperature sensitivity: if sigma changes rapidly over T, prefer multiplicative temperature factors (exp(c*T), exp(c/(T+c0))) on hardening/yield terms rather than only additive linear T shifts.
- Monotonicity constraints: most metals/polymers under monotonic loading have sigma increasing with epsilon at fixed T and decreasing with T at fixed epsilon; structure selection should preserve these monotonic trends via coefficient signs.

3) \(1.33613\,\epsilon\,(T-327.264\ldots)^2\) (linear in \(\epsilon\) times a **quadratic in \(T\) with a shift**)

So any matching candidate must be able (possibly after setting some parameters to 0) to reproduce:
- a standalone \(\epsilon^3\) term,
- an \(\epsilon^{0.214...}\exp(-K/T)\) term (exponential of reciprocal \(T\), not \(\exp(T\cdot)\)),
- and an \(\epsilon\cdot (T-\text{const})^2\) term (quadratic polynomial in \(T\), shifted).

Now check candidates.

But the remaining terms are \(T\epsilon^2\), \(T\epsilon\), \(|\epsilon|^{c3}\), \(\epsilon^2\), \(\epsilon\). There is **no way to create** \(\epsilon(T-327.264)^2 = \epsilon(T^2-2\cdot327.264\,T+327.264^2)\) because candidate has at most linear-in-\(T\) terms (\(T\epsilon\), \(T\epsilon^2\)) and no \(T^2\epsilon\). **No match**.

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + 1.336*epsilon*(T - 327.264)**2`

Let me expand the last term:
`epsilon*(T - 327.264)**2 = epsilon*(T² - 654.529*T + 107,102.0)`
So: `1.336*epsilon*T² - 873.65*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

Wait, but the GT has `epsilon*(T-c7)**2` which expands to `epsilon*T² - 2*c7*epsilon*T + c7²*epsilon`. So the GT contains terms: `c6*epsilon*T²`, `c6*(-2*c7)*epsilon*T`, and `c6*c7²*epsilon`.

So GT = `c0*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon**c3*exp(-c4/(c5*T)) + c6*epsilon*T² - 2*c6*c7*epsilon*T + c6*c7²*epsilon`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `epsilon**3` (polynomial)
2. `epsilon**c3*exp(-c4/(c5*T))` (fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type exponential)
3. `epsilon*T²` 
4. `epsilon*T`
5. `epsilon`

Note: Term 3 has `epsilon*T²`, which is `T*epsilon² * (T/epsilon)` — wait, let me re-read. The GT has `epsilon*c6*(T-c7)**c8` with c8=2. So it's `epsilon*(T-c7)²` = `epsilon*T² - 2c7*epsilon*T + c7²*epsilon`.

So the GT requires:
- `epsilon*T²` term
- `epsilon*T` term  
- `epsilon` term
- `epsilon**3` term
- `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-82.437/(8.314*T))` — an Arrhenius exponential in 1/T

Now let me check candidates. Most candidates have `T*epsilon**2` instead of `epsilon*T²`. These are different! `T*epsilon²` ≠ `epsilon*T²`. The GT needs `epsilon*T²` but most candidates only have `T*epsilon²`.

Wait — I need to re-examine. `epsilon*T²` means epsilon times T-squared. `T*epsilon²` means T times epsilon-squared. These are fundamentally different functions of two variables. So any candidate that only has `T*epsilon²` (and not `epsilon*T²`) cannot match GT.

Looking at ALL candidates: every single one has `T*c*epsilon**2` as a term (or similar), but NONE have `epsilon*T**2`. The GT requires `epsilon*T**2` as a basis function.

Let me double-check: Could any candidate produce `epsilon*T²`? Looking through all candidates, I see terms like `T*epsilon**2`, `T*epsilon`, `T**(1/3)*...`, `T**c*...`, but no `T**2*epsilon` term anywhere.

Without the `epsilon*T²` basis function, no candidate can match the GT. The functions `T*epsilon²` and `T²*epsilon` are linearly independent — they cannot substitute for each other.

Let me verify there's no clever way to combine terms to get `epsilon*T²`. For instance, could `T*epsilon²` combined with other terms produce `epsilon*T²`? No — these are monomials in different variables and are linearly independent.

Therefore, none of the candidates can match the GT.
